for British students,

3 Ifyou had to find a work placement, how would you go about it?
Experience matters —
How you can benefit from a work placement
A work placement is a fantastic opportunity to
gain some work experience and it is likely to be
very helpful for your future career. In the UK,
one or two-week formal work placements are
arranged either by schools or by the students
themselves. Some people think that‘ work experi-
ence’ only refers to these short work placements,
but any form of work you do before you start a
job, whether it is voluntary or paid, is useful work
experience.
Even if it doesn’t last long, work experience gives
you taste of what it's like to work in a particular
job or industry. You will gain practical experience
and learn new skills which will put you in a
stronger position when you apply for a job.
In many cases, work placement opportunities
are not advertised, so you need to be proactive
and to make use of your connections. Or you can
© /-E TEE
approach companies directly to find out if they
offer work placement opportunities.
Apart from work placements organized by schools,
there are also a lot of other things you can do to
learn about the world of work and experience it
first-hand
Volunteering is one way to get a good insight
into a particular job, area or industry. If you
are interested in animals and nature, we can
recommend interesting internships or projects
for volunteers abroad. For example, why not take
part in a scientific research project that deals
with the conservation of reptiles, insects and
sea turtles in Costa Rica? Or you could volunteer
with an organization that helps refugees and
migrants in Southern Italy. These organizations
need a lot of support in many different areas
such as community work, food distribution, event
organization and helping migrants with their
daily activities.
Of course, it is a good idea to look for placements
that will help you gain skills you will actually
need in your future job. So, for example, if you
already know that you want to work in logistics,
it would be a good idea to find a placement with
Welcome to the world of work
impressed when they see that, and who knows
There is always the possibility that one of these
firms might hire you once you've finished school
or college.
Employers are very keen on work experience
because it helps them to assess your character,
skills and work ethic - so don't miss this oppor
a transport company. Employers are usually
tunity
to impress them!

Im Rahmen des Workshops bekommen Sie ein Handout zum Thema ,Global mobility’,
das für Ihre Firma interessant sein könnte.
Lesen Sie das Handout und machen Sie sich auf Deutsch Notizen zu folgenden Punkten:
Warum wird das Thema „Globale Mobilität“ für Arbeitgeber immer wichtiger?
Warum wird Arbeiten im Ausland für Arbeitnehmer zunehmend attraktiv?
Was muss ein Arbeitgeber bedenken, wenn er Arbeitnehmer ins Ausland schickt?
Was ist der wesentliche Unterschied zwischen den beiden Möglichkeiten, Arbeitnehmer
ins Ausland zu entsenden?
Welche der beiden Optionen wird bei zeitlich befristeten Aufenthalten meistens gewählt?
Warum kann es für einen Arbeitnehmer attraktiv sein, befristet im Ausland zu arbeiten?
Global mobility
There is an increasing trend towards profes-
sional mobility. But what does this development
mean for companies and employees?
It's clear that the number of people taking up a
post abroad is increasing steadily. For companies,
mobility is becoming more and more important
because of global markets. And for employees,
working abroadisa great opportunity to enhance
their professional skills, which gives them an
advantage when they apply for a new job.
However, if someone intends to work abroad,
or a company wants to send an employee on a
foreign assignment, they need to be well pre
pared. It is best to get expert advice on any for-
malities that might be necessary.
There are several things a company needs to
think about when sending employees abroad.
First of all, how long will they be working abroad?
Secondly, where will they be working and what
kind of status will they have? And finally, what
is the best solution for both company and em-
ployee in terms of protection and cost?
Basically, there are two options: the first is the
posting of employees abroad, also called second-
ment. This means that the employee works for
another ‘host’ organization on a temporary basis
and returns to their original employer once the
posting is finished. Within the EU, employees
can be abroad on posted status for up to two
experience
CAREER
WORK *=
ABROAD
OPPORTUNITY
future
WORKING
NEW a —
years. Why choose this option? There can be
many reasons,
for example to help the candidate
with their career development or to gain more
experience or skills in a local subsidiary or af-
filiated company. It also offers employees the
chance to work on short-term projects abroad.
Employees posted abroad keep their employment
contract and remain employees of the home
company.
The second possibility is to suspend or terminate
an employee's contract with the home company
so that he or she can be employed by the host
company abroad. In this case, there is no direct
relationship between employee and home coun-
‘try orhome company. This type of arrangement is
not a posting. Companies sometimes choose this
option when they have a specific job to do abroad
and recruit a person for a specific assignment.
(358 Wörter)

Tim,
Düsseldorf
Wenn man im Ausland arbeitet, hat man immer mit einer Sprachbarriere zu kämpfen
- auch wenn man die
Sprache gut spricht. Ich habe zwei Monate lang ein Praktikum in einem Transportunternehmen in London
gemacht, und es fiel mir anfangs sehr schwer, meine Kollegen
zu verstehen und mit ihnen zu sprechen. Sie haben
sehr schnell gesprochen und viele Redewendungen und Ausdrücke benutzt, die ich noch nie gehört hatte.
Ich musste sie oft bitten, Dinge zu wiederholen, was mir anfangs peinlich war. Aber ich muss sagen, sie waren
sehr freundlich und hilfsbereit, und gegen Ende meines Aufenthaltes war die Kommunikation viel einfacher!
Anna, Gelsenkirchen
Ich habe ein Jahr lang in Frankreich gearbeitet. Das Land fand ich toll, aber die ersten Wochen waren wirklich hart!
Es wurde besser, sobald ich meine Kollegen etwas näher kennenlernte und einige Freunde fand, mit denen ich
nach der Arbeit zusammen sein konnte. Es ist nicht so einfach, neue Freunde im Ausland zu finden, und außerdem
war es für mich schwer, so lange von meiner Familie und meinen Freunden getrennt zu sein. Ich hatte Heimweh
und vermisste sie sehr. Sicher, du kannst über Videochat in Kontakt bleiben, aber du brauchst auch jemanden, mit
dem du reden kannst und der dir helfen kann, wenn du ein Problem hast. Wenn man ins Ausland geht, sollte
man deshalb nicht vergessen, dass es Herausforderungen geben wird - es scheint nicht jeden Tag die Sonne!
Georg, Hückeswagen
Wenn man ins Ausland geht, weiß man, dass es kulturelle Unterschiede zwischen dem Heimatland und dem
Gastland gibt. Aber ich glaube, man erkennt sie erst richtig, wenn man da ist. Ich habe sechs Monate in Sevilla
verbracht. In den ersten Tagen war ich um 8.00 Uhr im Büro, aber es war niemand da. Es dauerte eine Weile,
bis mir klar wurde, dass die Leute hier erst gegen 9.30 Uhr mit der Arbeit beginnen, was ich für sehr spät hielt.
Dann haben wir gegen 13 Uhr immer mindestens eine Stunde lang zusammen gegessen. Siesta ist nicht mehr
so verbreitet, aber
es gibt noch Büros,
die am Nachmittag eine längere Pause einlegen. Das bedeutet,
dass die
‘Menschen abends länger arbeiten. Ich fand meine Zeit in Spanien
toll, aber ich fand es nicht gut, so lange im
Büro bleiben zu müssen. Ich bin nie vor 19 oder 20 Uhr gegangen.
(a12 wörter)

[=] EQUAL WAGES - BUT NOT FOR EVERYONE
You are going to watch an interview with Henrike von Platen, an activist for equal pay and the founder
of Fair Pay Innovation Lab.
Before watching
the video match the phrases in the
list to the correct explanations.
equal pay for equal work + gender wage gap +
glass ceiling + sticky floor - pink-collar jobs
Onaverage, women stay longer in low-level
positions and must wait longer for promotions
than men.
2 Women often cannot progress beyond a
certain point on the career ladder. They are
not promoted to the highest levels of a
company or they only reach these levels
with great difficulty.
3 Pay disparity (the difference between men
and women’s average wages) is often
represented as a percentage.
4 Everyone who performs the same job should
be paid equally.
5 Jobs in sectors that are considered traditionally
‘female’ are low-paying or even unpaid

Work-life balance is out
Young employees will only stay at firms offering ‘work-
Nowadays, it's so hard to find people to work at
German companies that they are offering new
employees longer holidays, shorter working
hours, flexible shifts and sabbaticals. This is
happening in a country where people already
have the shortest working hours of all developed
countries.
When Deutsche Bahn, one of the country's big
gest employers, offered its workforce a choice
between six days extra paid holiday, a 2.6% pay
rise ora one-hour cut in the working week, most
(58%) chose the extra holiday. That meant that
Deutsche Bahn workers who already got 30 days
paid holiday a year increased this total to 36.
Only 2% of employees chose Deutsche Bahn’s
offer of
a one-hour cut in working hours because
German workers already have one of the short
est working weeks in the western world. OECD“
statistics show that in 2016 the average German
worked 1363 hours per year. In the other
35 OECD
countries,
the average working hours were 1,763
per year with the US at 1,783 and Mexico leading
ife-life balance’.

Work is no longer the top priority for young

was a ‘work-life-life-life’ capital because young

In the workplace
Mission impossible?
The truth about being an online delivery driver
Revealed: delivery giant Hermes pays some couriers less than living wage
Britain's second-biggest parcel company, Hermes,
which delivers for John Lewis and other major
retailers, is paying some of its couriers at levels
equivalent to below the national living wage
according to a snapshot of information provided
by some of those who have worked there.
[..] Hermes does not need to pay its couriers the
£720 an hour living wage introduced in April
because they are self-employed. [..] One self.
employed courier for Hermes provided evidence
that suggested she took home approximately
£5.90 an hour over two weeks of recent work and
another showed invoice data that indicated she
earned no more than £6.70 per hour.
A third courier provided estimates that she
earned £5,50 per hour over nine days. All three of
those who delivered parcels said they worked six
days a week, from three to six hours per day.
‘Two couriers also showed the Guardian accounts
from 12 months of work. One calculated he had
eared about £7.30 per hour in the last tax year
and that was without any paid holiday or sick
pay and without pension contributions. Another
earned about £6.90 per hour over the same year.
Hermes said that according to its calculations,
based partly on its own estimates of the time
needed to deliver parcels, none of its couriers are
‘earning below the ‘national
living wage’ It said it
is monitoring several hundred couriers who it
believes are earning “around £7.20 per hour to
ensure they do not drop further’
Hermes has contracts with 10,500 people paid
on a piecework basis to deliver parcels using
their own cars. Dubbed ‘lifestyle couriers, they
are self-employed and so do not receive any paid
holiday, sick pay, parental leave or pension
contributions.
They pay for their own fuel and car insurance
but are free to take other jobs and have some
flexibility over their working day. They are part
of the fast growing ‘gig economy’ in which big
companies, including Hermes, rely on increasing
numbers of self-employed contractors, who are
not subject to the national living wage, to deliver
their core services.
(858 words)
Source: www.theguardian.com/society/2016/jul/18/
+hermes-couriers-paying_staff-less-than-living-wage

Mediation,
Trend towards freelancing
Meaning of the term ‘gig economy’
Advantages for employers
Formalities, hourly rates and flexibility
Insurance, car maintenance costs, shifts and payment unclear
Gig-Economy: Selbststandig unselbststandig
Selbstandig sein? Unabhangig? Den Arbeitstag
nach den eigenen Vorlieben planen? Willkom
men in der neuen digitalen Arbeitswelt, in der
jeder sein eigener Unternehmer sein kann und
umständliche Bürokratie der Vergangenheit an
gehört: Einfach App runterladen, beim Anbieter
registrieren, und schon lockt ein Verdienst an
geblich weit über dem Mindestlohn von aktuell
9,19 Euro pro Stunde.
Und so sieht man sie längst durch die Stadt flit-
zen: die Essenkuriere von App-basierten Diens
ten, deren Auslieferer mit dem eigenen Fahrrad
fahren müssen, oder Paketzusteller, die ihr Privat-
auto nutzen, um Bestellungen auszufahren.
Diese Selbständigen hangeln sich von Auftrag
zu Auftrag und sind damit Teil der sogenannt-
en Gig-Economy. Der Begriff Gig stammt aus
der Musikszene und bezeichnet eigentlich den
Auftritt von Musikern, wobei der Auftraggeber
sie nach Leistung und Bedarf beschäftigt und
bezahlt
Schon seit vordigitalen Zeiten umgehen Unter-
nehmen unangenehme Arbeitgeberpflichten, in-
dem sie beispielsweise Paketboten nicht festan-
stellen, sondern zu Subunternehmern machen.
So spart das Unternehmen Sozialkosten, und die
Boten sieht man dann ihre Pakete im Laufschritt
zustellen.
Ein amerikanischer Internet-Handelsriese über-
trägt dieses Prinzip nun ins Zeitalter der Gig-
Economy mit einem eigenen Zustelldienst: Selbst-
ständige sollen mit ihrem Privatauto Bestellun-
gen ausfahren. Bedingung ist, dass man voll-
jährig sein, einen Führerschein und ein Smart-
phone haben muss. In Aussicht gestellt wird ein
„Stundenlohn bis zu 25 Euro“, und die geforderte
Flexibilität diene dazu, „mehr Zeit zu haben, Ihre
Ziele und Träume zu verwirklichen”.
Dies klingt natürlich alles großartig, lenkt aller-
dings davon ab, dass die Unternehmens-Website
weder über den genauen Abrechnungsmodus
noch über Versicherungsregelungen oder Unter-
haltskosten für die Fahrzeuge informiert. Außer-
dem ist keine Vollzeittatigkeit garantiert, da die
Schichten schwanken können. Vielmehr wird der
Verdienst als Zusatzeinkommen angepriesen, das
man sich locker nebenher in der Freizeit erwirt-
schaften kann. Bleibt abzuwarten, ob die Gig
Economy das Beschaftigungsmodell der Zukunft
werden wird.
(295 words)

pes of business
orgar
Three ways to do business
UK: Sole trader
US: Sole proprietor
+ The company belongs to the sole trader.
+ The sole trader takes decisions alone.
+ He/She
gets all the profit.
+ He/She could lose everything.
UK: Private limited company (Ltd)*
US: Limited liability company (LLC)
+ The company belongs to a closed circle of
members.
+ The members decide what is best for the company.
+ The members share the profits.
+ The members can only lose the money they have
invested.
UK: Public limited company (plc)
US: Corporation (Corp./Inc.)
+ The company belongs to the shareholders, who are
members of the public.
The directors decide what is best for the company
and the shareholders.
The shareholders share the profits.
The shareholders can only lose the money they
paid for the shares.

SensorTech Stern Solutions Ltd is very aware of climate change and wants
to reduce its carbon footprint
and emissions in as many ways
as possible. You realize you need more background information and find
the following article online.
Skim the article then choose a suitable heading (a~f) for each paragraph (1-5). There is one more heading
than you need.
a Consequences of global warming
d Technology to stop global warming
b Explanation of carbon footprint
e The importance of greenhouse gases
© Howa greenhouse works
f Why there is global warming
1 To understand why your carbon footprint is so important, you first need
to understand how
a greenhouse works and what greenhouse gases are.
A greenhouse is a building with a roof and walls made
of glass in which
plants are grown. The glass lets in light from the sun. When sunlight hits a
solid surface, eg. earth or plants, it turns into heat. The darker
the surface,
the more heat is produced. Light enters the greenhouse through its glass
walls very easily. The heat it produces takes a lot longer to escape through
the glass of the greenhouse, so the greenhouse warms up.
rounded by greenhouse gases (mainly water vapour and carbon dioxide,
but also methane, nitrous oxide and ozone) which let the sunlight in quickly
but let the heat out slowly. Without greenhouse gases the temperature
on the Earth would be about
~18 °C. Greenhouse gases give us our climate
and, thanks to them, the average temperature of the Earth is about +15°C.
2 Instead of being surrounded by glass like a greenhouse, the Earth is sur-
3 For thousands of years there was a natural balance between sunlight,
animal life, forests and oceans, but since the Industrial Revolution (1750)
more and more carbon dioxide has entered the atmosphere because fossil
fuels producing carbon dioxide are used to power industry and transport.
Carbon emissions have increased by 45% since 1750, with the result that
‘more and more heat is trapped in the atmosphere and the Earth is warming
up. This is known as global warming,
4 Every person on the planet produces a so-called carbon footprint. This
is the total amount of the greenhouse gases, including carbon dioxide,
produced by everything that person does, uses and consumes. This means,
for example, what they eat and drink; the clothes they wear; the means
transport they use and how often they use them; where they work; where
and how they live; how the products they use are manufactured; what life-
style they have.
In the workplace
5 Inthe opinion of prominent scientists
and the United Nations, if we do
not reduce our carbon emissions drastically, the Earth’s surface temperature
will be 2°C higher by 2036. The result will be more extreme weather
conditions such as hurricanes
and droughts; animal and plant life will be
endangered; the polar ice caps will melt even faster than is already the
case and low-lying
areas will be flooded. For this reason, itis important
understand our carbon footprint and reduce our carbon emissions, so the
Earth's temperature does not rise by 15°C, after which the consequences
(424 words)
will be irreversible.

OUTSOURCING: Der flexible Weg für Mittelständler
Outsourcing ist längst gängige Praxis in kleinen
und mittelstandischen Unternehmen. Und das
mit gutem Grund: Werden ausgewählte Aufgaben
an externe Dienstleistungsunternehmen abgege-
ben, können Sie in zweierlei Hinsicht profitieren.
- _ Stärken Sie Ihr Kerngeschäft und ermöglichen
Sie Ihren Mitarbeitern und Mitarbeiterinnen,
sich auf das Wesentliche zu konzentrieren.
Sparen Sie langfristig Kosten, indem Sie
Dienstleister ans Werk lassen, welche die
Arbeit schneller, effizienter und oftmals
besser verrichten können. (..)
Outsourcing-Vorteile ergeben sich in mehreren
Gebieten: Gängige Bereiche, die Sie einem ver
trauensvollen Kooperationspartner in die Hände
geben können, sind
 dasIT-Wesen,
das Human-Resource-Management,
die Logistik,
die Buchhaltung und
das Gebäudemanagement.
Auslagerung:
Überlassen Sie es den Profis
Ein Spezialist arbeitet in der Regel effektiv und ef-
fizient. Einer der Outsoureing-Vorteile ist deshalb,
dass Aufgaben extern besser erledigt werden kön-
nen als durch interne Maßnahmen Folglich steigt
bei Auslagerung die Qualität der Arbeit. (..)
Ist beispielsweise der Drucker defekt, kann ein
ungelernter Mitarbeiter Stunden damit verbrin
gen, das Gerät wieder zum Laufen zu bringen.
Die Tüftelei kostet Ihre Firma Zeit und Geld.
Fällt der Server aus, dürfte selbst der ambitio
nierteste Hobby-Techniker mit seinem Latein
am Ende sein. Ein Profi hat das Problem im
besten Fall mit wenigen Handgriffen gelöst,
ohne Arbeitsabläufe zu verzögern. (..)
Outsourcing-Nachteile: Es gibt auch Risiken
Führen Sie sich Outsourcing Vorteile vor Augen,
sollten Sie selbstverständlich ebenfalls die Nach-
teile der Auslagerung kennen. Dazu gehören
Abhängigkeit vom Dienstleister und
zusätzlicher Kommunikationsaufwand.
Um die Outsourcing-Vorteile zu genießen, bege-
ben Sie sich in eine Abhängigkeit, das bedeutet:
Macht Ihr Dienstleister einen Fehler oder
hater Probleme, müssen Sie die Misere unter
Umständen ausbaden.
Sobald Ihr Partner die Preise anhebt, müssen
Sie zahlen, selbst wenn Sie mit anderen Kos-
ten gerechnet haben.
Betriebsgeheimnisse sind nicht mehr so
sicher wie vorher. (..)
Ein weiterer potenzieller Stolperstein: die Kom-
munikation. Bereits intern ist es keine leichte
‚Aufgabe, sich verständlich, präzise und korrekt
zu verständigen. Bei einer Auslagerung von Auf.
gaben an einen externen Kooperationspartner
wird es sogar noch schwieriger. Vor allem, sobald
sich Gesprächspartner nur übers Telefon oder das
Internet austauschen.

The new generation of consumers
‘Manufacturers and providers of products and services need to know their market, and a growing part
of the market is Generation Z. This generation should not be confused with millennials. Millennials
RECERIOGHNIT DUES AOE
are the generation born roughly between 1980 and 1995 who know what the world was like before
the internet reached into every part of our lives. Generation Z, however, who were born after 1995,
only know a world where the internet and mobile technology is normal and a fact of life. For this
generation there is no distinction between online and offline: just as your arms and legs are parts of
your body, the internet and the real world are simply parts of your everyday experience. So, let's get
to know this generation of Americans better in terms
of how they consume products and services.

They want to get to know you better
Product or service — is there a difference?
1) The first and most basic difference is that a
product is tangible. It is
a physical thing you can
touch or hold that a company made, or grew,
to sell to you. A service, on the other hand, is
something that you pay a company to do for you.
As such, it is not something you can touch or
hold It is intangible. (While banks and insurance
companies may advertise their products, in
reality they offer financial services and are
included in the services industry)
2) Products are designed and manufactured,
or grown, to meet a particular need. You need
a hammer? Go into a hardware store and buy
one - your need is met. Services should also
meet a customer's needs, but - and here is the
big difference - you, the customer, cannot
separate the service or yourself from the service
provider. There is a relationship between you
and the service provider, and that relationship
is key. A good service provider should use that
relationship to get to know its clients better
and be ready to tailor its service quickly to its
customers’ changing requirements.
TEEo
3) Intoday's world, itis hard to tell products apart.
Think of your smartphone
—is there really some-
thing your phone can do that a friend's phone from
a different manufacturer cannot? Probably not.
Some phone makers experimented with custom-
izable smartphones where users could choose
different hardware modules, but the increased
costs in materials and multiple production lines
made it too costly. Instead, in an attempt to stand
out from the crowd, manufacturers have turned
to the services that they can bundle with their
products, because services, being intangible, are
much cheaper and easier to modify. This has led
to the distinction between product and service
becoming almost meaningless.
4) This is the concept of a product as a service.
This idea sees products as gateways to the
‘ecosystem’ of related services provided by the
manufacturer and its strategic partners. Based
oncurrent technological developments,
this trend
is only going to continue. Television makers today
not only want you to buy their latest ultra-high-
definition flat screen, but they also want you
to sign up for the subscription TV and game
streaming service which comes pre-installed
on the smart TV. And who needs a separate TV
remote control when you can download the TV
manufacturer's free smartphone app that will do
it for you? As we enter the age of the Internet of
Things, every electronicitem bought, whetheritis
a bedside lamp, refrigerator or washing machine,
provides an opportunity for a company to estab
lish an ongoing relationship with the purchaser
and leam more about their customers toimprove
their services and also find out what other
products or services they could need.
5) As part of this effort, manufacturers
are turn
to the loss-leader strategy that supermarkets
have long used, i. selling a popular product at a
Products and services
very low price to attract customers in the hope
that they purchase other items on their shopping
list. Manufacturers offer their core products at
lower prices on the condition that you sign up to
pay a monthly or annual fee for the other services
they offer. Printer manufacturers, for example,
make a short-term loss on their printers, but a
longer-term profit on the extra services they
provide such as ink replacement or over-the-air
printing. This has the added benefit of ‘locking
in’those customers for longer periods
—a form of
guaranteed brand loyalty. This can also mean
that the retailer is removed from the relation
ship with the customer, helping the producer to
strengthen its direct relationship with consumers
through its own website.
(ext)
© Ecosystem describes the plants and creatures that live in a particular area. The word can also be
used to describe the extra services and products that are connected to, and only work with, a technology
company's core systems and platforms.

Das Abonnement-Preismodell ist ein boomendes und erfolgreiches Geschäft, das sich besonders
Softwareentwickler eignet. Dennoch gibt es einige Risiken zu beachten. Wie kann ein Unternehmen den
Übergang von einem All-In-One-Produkt-Modell zu einem Abo-Modell bewältigen?
Einige Unternehmen konzentrieren sich zu stark auf die Gewinnung neuer Kunden. Aber was diese
Unternehmen zu ihrem Nachteil vergessen, ist ihr bestehender Kundenstamm. Betrachten wir den
Kunden, der im Oktober in ein neues Softwaresystem investiert und im Dezember eine Marketing-E-Mail
erhält, in der steht, dass seine „neue“ Software im nächsten Jahr nicht mehr unterstützt wird und er
You are getting some work experience at Schmidt & Grüntuch Steuersoftware
GmbH. The company publishes CD-ROMs with computer software for tax accountants
and private
consumers, but now they are considering changing to a subscription pricing business model
sich für ein neues Abo-Preismodell anmelden muss. Dieser Kunde ist wahrscheinlich bald ein Ex-Kunde.
filo
‘Scenario support, S. 188
Also ist der Verlust
treuer Kunden ein Risiko, das Unternehmen unbedingt vermeiden müssen.
Das sogenannte Fischmodell zeigt die kurzfristigen Auswirkungen der Geschaftsmodellumstellung
auf die Kosten und Erträge eines Unternehmens. So können die Umsätze während der Umstellung bei
iden
Kosten

sinken.

Products and services
a failure to adapt led to the death of a giant
You are doing an internship with Messaging Ltd, the advertising agency that is responsible for the
marketing mix
for the Inspired smartpen.
In 2007, one Finnish company enjoyed a 49.4%
share of the mobile phone market. Yet in 2013,
that same company’s market share had shrunk
to just 3% and the company’s failing phone
manufacturing business was bought by a top PC
software company. Where did it all go wrong
for the mobile phone giant Nokia?
One of the biggest factors in the failure was the
company’s strategy. The brand was famous for its
devices, and while smaller and smaller mobiles
were trendy in the 1990s and the built-in game
‘Snake’ was popular worldwide,
this was the pre-
smartphone era. When the simple rectangular
iPhone was launched in 2007, phones became
‘smart. Mobile apps were born. These new
devices all looked similar - customers weren't
buying a device now, but the services and
platforms that could synchronize and organize
their new online, digital lives. The Finnish
company, however, kept its focus on devices
and hardware. They failed to develop a software
ecosystem, their own products had different
operating systems, 57 different systems by 2009.
This meant their products took longer to develop
and make. Once loyal customers stopped waiting
and moved to other smartphone brands.
Another major reason was a leadership failure.
In an attempt to become more flexible and
responsive to the shorter and shorter product
life cycles in mobile technology, the company
decided to restructure its workforce. Product
development teams that had worked quite
independently in the past were now expected to
work as one. A lack of communication between
the company’s senior bosses and its workers
meant these changes came as a shock. Creative
teams were broken up, experienced workers
became angry and left the company, while those
who stayed became demotivated. This robbed
the giant of its greatest assets - its brains and
creative spark.
The giant struggled on. Its brand became un-
fashionable and its market share grew smaller
and smaller. Profits turned to huge losses and
tens of thousands of workers lost their jobs.
‘The giant was now an old and weak shadow of
itself. In 2013, the Finnish brand disappeared asa
maker
of mobile phones,
never to appear again
Until 2016 that is, when an ex-director of the
company bought the rights to its name and
classic designs and re-entered the smartphone
market. At the time of writing, it had built up a
1% share of the world market.
(au words)

--- Seite 57 ---
‘A marketing expert named E. Jerome McCarthy defined the
4 Ps in the 1960s. They have been used and
developed since then as the so-called ‘marketing mix’ in order
to help businesses create new products
or services for their customers.
Read this text about the 4 Ps and decide where sentences A-D should go.
A Itcan also affect how a product is seen by customers because it is an indicator of value.
Businesses should also consider how they plan to develop it after its launch to ensure that
it has along and profitable life.
C However, if one of these goes wrong, a company’s reputation and a product's image can be
destroyed very quickly.
D_Andif customers purchase online, the goods or services still need to be delivered to them
P for product: Product covers everything to do with the creation, development and management of
products or services. It's not only about what to make but when and how to make it and above all what
the unique selling point of the product is.
1 Development of the product's next iteration - or version —
should always be a priority. Furthermore, a product is not just a physical thing It includes intangible
add-ons such as after-sales service, guarantees, installation and maintenance anything that helps to
distinguish the product from the competition and make the customer more likely to buy it.
P for price: Price is not perhaps as simple as it seems. Price doesn't only refer to the production costs
Plus the mark-up a business adds on top to generate a profit. 2 Pricing a product too low could send
a message to customers that it is of low value and cheaply made. On the other hand, pricing the goods
too high - especially if it is a new product or from a new manufacturer - could stop people from buying
it. Pricing strategies include discounts on large orders, lower prices for early adopters of new products
or services, and subscription pricing models, which are becoming increasingly common. It is critical
that the pricing strategy is right for the product's target market.
P for place: Place means simply where your target customers can find the product - whether in a
physical bricks-and-mortar store or online. The product must be positioned and distributed in places
where its target market can buy it. 3 Logistics, distribution channels and the retailers involved in
getting the product to the right place at the right time for the end consumer are all key components
of place. Recent developments in this area include so-called ‘pop-up’ stores which appear in empty
retail spaces or at special events and disappear after a short period.
P for promotion: Promotion is about advertising and communication and often involves publicity and
high-profile activities which can successfully persuade customers to hand over their money. 4 Ofthe
four Ps, promotion has been most affected by the internet, in particular by social media. Search Engine
Optimization (SEO) - getting your product and brand to the top of the results page in an internet
search —is an absolute must these days. The rise of social media influencers and the fact that traditional
word-of-mouth advertising can now be read online by millions of internet users mean that social
media needs wise and constant analysis, planning and management.
(415 words)

Scenario support, 5.189
Ein englischsprachiger Kollege ist der Ansicht, dass der Trend, auf Kunststoff komplett zu
verzichten, zu extrem sei. Sie möchten mehr zum Thema herausfinden, um mit ihm besser darüber
diskutieren zu können. Sie finden einen interessanten Text in Internet.
Fassen Sie die wichtigsten Aspekte des Textes unter den folgenden Überschriften auf Englisch zusammen:
- The environmental impact of glass bottles
+ The benefits of plastic packaging in avoiding food wastage
+ The factors that contribute to the environmental footprint of packaging materials
Heutzutage gilt als unumstritten, dass Kunststoffverpackungen belastend für die Umwelt sind —
besonders, wenn es sich um Einwegverpackungen handelt und noch mehr, wenn sie lange Trans-
portwege hinter sich haben. Aus diesem Grund verfolgen viele Einzelhändler und Supermärkte seit
einiger Zeit eine Null-Verpackungspolitik. Einige Kunststoffproduzenten behaupten jedoch, dass dies
hauptsächlich auf den aktuellen „Greenwashing”-Trend zurückzuführen sei - d.h. umweltfreundlich
zu erscheinen, ohne es wirklich zu sein. Der Interessenverband American Plastics Federation geht
sogar so weit zu behaupten, dass eine vollständige Abkehr von Kunststoffverpackungen viel umwelt-
schädlicher sei.
Der Verband zeigt am Beispiel von Flaschen, dass Gasflaschen in der Herstellung zwar günstiger als
Kunststoffflaschen,
jedoch zehnmal so schwer sind. Das höhere Gewicht hat zur Folge, dass für den
Transport von Glasflaschen vierzig Prozent mehr Energie benötigt wird, während des Transports mehr
Kohlendioxid entsteht und die Transportkosten fünfmal höher als bei Kunststoffflaschen sind. So
seien dem Verband zufolge beim Gebrauch von Glasflaschen die Auswirkungen auf die Umwelt viel
drastischer.
TeEo%
Products and services
Als weiteres Beispiel führt die American Plastics Federation Lebensmittelabfälle an. Gurken ohne Ver
packung halten sich bei Aufbewahrung außerhalb eines Kühlschranks zwei Tage, bei Lagerung im
Kühlschrank neun Tage. Mit Kunststoffverpackungen können Gurken im Kühlschrank bis zu fünfzehn
Tage frisch bleiben. Bei Fleisch seien die Vorteile von Kunststoffverpackungen noch deutlicher, heißt
es.In versiegelten Kunststoffschalen kann Fleisch zwischen drei und sieben Tage lang frisch bleiben, bei
Verwendung von Kunststoff-Vakuumverpackungen sogar bis zu 45 Tage lang. Bessere Kunststoff-Schutz-
Verpackungen können so den Abfall von unverkauften oder beschädigten Lebensmitteln reduzieren,
bei Fleisch seien dies vierzig Prozent.
Dies zeigt, dass Verpackungen aus anderen Materialien nicht zwangsläufig eine bessere Ökobilanz
als Kunststoffverpackungen haben. Wichtig sind Faktoren wie Aufwand bei der Herstellung des
Materials, Transportweg und Entsorgung bzw. Häufigkeit der Wiederverwendungen. Denn um zu
beurteilen, wie umweltfreundlich eine Verpackung wirklich ist, muss immer ihr gesamter Lebensweg
betrachtet werden.

PROMOTING ALTERNATIVES — PACKAGE-FREE RETAIL
Increasing numbers of retailers across Europe
are renouncing single-use plastic packaging
selling more of their products loose or with
refillable containers. Efforts to reduce waste and
single-use plastic packaging can be seen in
different aspects of food retail
Distribution: a French retailer introduced 18
million reusable packing crates for fruit and
vegetables. Reverse logistics on these crates is
supported by electronic chips, which allow
retailers to track their crates and produce
throughout the distribution chain. Cases are
rented rather than owned by the retailer, saving
150 tonnes of waste annually and reducing
emissions by 30% compared to previous
distribution methods.
Inside the store: more retailers are selling
goods loose or with minimal packaging. A key
challenge is to eliminate single-use plastic
bags, plastic straws and single-use coffee cups
among independent retailers.

Reviews and feedback enable a customer-focused approach
Work quickly on an idea
- do only what's necessary, not more
Traditional product development was time-consuming
Modern goods can be easily updated without changing the tangible product
watch the video. Decide if the following statements are true or false according to the video. Correct the
false statements.
Traditional product development took just as long in the past as it does today.
These days, a version of a product can be brought to market in a very short time.
A minimum viable product is made quickly and cheaply, but only has the basic features.
A sprint is when a team works quickly on an idea and doesn’t do more than is needed.
Iterative design means repeatedly updating a product even after it has been launched.
It is not important to finish a product when using an iterative design approach.
Reviews and feedback help customers to focus on the company's iterative approach.
Noununa
El think about the question at the end of the video:
‘The need for faster development cycles has hit almost all industries, what's it like where you work?"
Write a short paragraph in answer to the question. Use examples from your work experience or from
products that you know and use regularly.

>> Rez
Welche zwei Dinge ermöglichen es den Unternehmen, immer mehr Daten über das Kunden-
verhalten zu sammeln?
2 Warum stimmen McDonald zufolge viele Verbraucher Vereinbarungen zu, die den Unternehmen
das Datensammeln ermöglichen?
3 Welche Anhaltspunkte liefert McDonald dafür, dass die Verbraucher immer weniger Auswahl
auf dem Markt haben?
4 Was rät McDonald den Verbrauchern?
Are we heading for a future of less freedom and less choice?
Juliana McDonald is the author
of a new book called “The Surveillance Market’ and her main argument isthat
the ultimate aim of modern capitalism is not to automate production, but to automate ...us, the customers.
McDonald believes that from the beginning of the new millennium, the technology giants of Silicon
Valley have been perfecting ways of gathering information and learning about customer behaviour.
All of this information, she says, is now being used to develop ‘prediction products’ — these ‘products
can anticipate
what you~ the customer
- will do now, soon and in the future.
The rise of smart products - home speakers, video camera doorbells, wearables including even smart
clothes ~ has enabled companies to gather ever more information on what we do and where and when
we do it. The trend towards everything-as-a-service is also giving companies detailed information about
how we use the services we pay for. While some of this information is used to improve and develop these
services, there is
a lot more behavioural data that companies
are gathering about us that is not directly
related to the services we pay for. McDonald says that this process has turned people's lives and experience
into human ‘raw materials’ that companies trade in.
But don't
we consumers know
this already? No, she says. People are signing
away their rights when they
click ‘Accept’ to user agreements that they never fully read because they are too long and written in legal
language. Is there a reason
to fear these developments? McDonald says that we should. While consumer
society should normally consist of a free market with freedom of choice for the consumer, McDonald
believes our freedom of choice is being destroyed. She gives the example of online news apps. Knowing
what users read in real time, news apps provide
a ‘Most read’ summary of news stories and then readers
start getting their news straight from that section, rather than choosing freely what to read.
The same process is happening elsewhere. In 2019, one internet search engine had eighty-eight per cent
of the search market, one online marketplace had fifty per cent of the US e-commerce market, one social
media company controlled two-thirds of its market while two mobile phone manufacturers had half the
market between them. According to McDonald,
this all points to a decrease in choice for the consumer
driven by firms knowing much more about
What can we do about it? McDonald says that we are in the middle of a revolution and, being in the middle,
we cannot clearly see how
it will end. But we must wake up to this consumer culture of surveillance,
people and their governments
must protect personal data before we are in a future where companies
know’ what we want before we want it and where consumers and society become less free as a result
Let us know what you think by leaving your comments below.
(492 words)
“Smart devices - blessing or curse?’ Write a comment on this question.

Commercial correspondence
Business letter layout
‘About 360 million people speak English as their first language and many more use it for business,
so there is no standard layout for business letters. A typical layout used in Europe and elsewhere is
shown opposite
1 Letterhead
The letterhead should include
the sender's name, postal address including the country, telephone
fax numbers, email address and website address. It often also has the company's logo.
Reference
Tina Lorenz (TL) signed the letter and someone
whose initials are
BK (e.g. Bernd Knopf) typed it. Some
companies have different reference systems (e.g. Ref. 1/L 21.4000)
Date
An all-figure date can be misunderstood. in American English 08/09/22 (or 08-09-22) means August 09,
2022 but in British English it means
08 September 2022. For this reason,
the month should always be
written out and the year should be a four-figure number. The usual order
in which a date is written in
business letters and forms is day
(in figures)
- month (as a word)
- year (in figures).
4 Special marking
These include URGENT
/ PRIVATE AND CONFIDENTIAL / PERSONAL
/ AIR MAIL / REGISTERED,
RECORDED DELIVERY. The special marking can be seen over the inside address (see below) in
a window envelope.
CONFIDENTIAL
McPakit Ltd
350 Portobello Road
EDINBURGH
EHISTAN
VEREINIGTES KÖNIGREICH
Attn. Ms McDermott, Marketing Department
window envelope
Inside address
This is the recipient's address. Always include the country if sending a letter abroad (in German if
the letter is being sent from Germany, e.g. IRLAND) because
the same city names can be found in
different countries. When writing to a UK address write the town or city in capital letters and the
postcode on a separate line under it.
6 Attention (Attn.)
The attention
line is under the inside address and close enough to it to be seen in a window envelope
(see above). if there is an attention line, the letter may be opened by the company's post department
and given to the person named. However, if the inside address starts with someone's name it may
only
be opened by that person or their secretary.

7/10 Salutation
/ Complimentary close
In most cases the salutation and complimentary close in both letters and emails can be written without
punctuation and they are linked as shown in the table below. In general, it is always better to write toa
named person than a company but if this is not possible, start the letter ‘Dear Sir or Madam’ and use
Yours faithfully’
as the complimentary close

 Subjectline
This is written in bold letters
or underlined. it starts with a capital letter. The rest of the line is written
in small letters, apart from proper names, geographical names, nationalities
and languages,
etc.
9 Body of the letter
The first word always starts with a capital letter. The paragraphs are separated by a free line.
10 Complimentary close
7 above. The name of the sender's company
is written under the complimentary
close.
11 Signature
Signatures are often hard to read, so write the signatory's name and position under the signature.
As there is no real English equivalent to Sachbearbeiter/in, itis best to name the department where the
signatory works (e.g. ‘Sales Department’
for Verkaufssachbearbeiter/in). Women can add their preferred
title in brackets after their name if they wish.
12 Enclosure(s)
Itis often enough just to write ‘Enc’ or ‘Encs’ but, if necessary, details
of the enclosure(s) can be listed
like this: ‘Enc: Contract’ or Encs: Contracts:

Commercial correspondence
Next you discuss an information sheet about the Incoterms® rules with a German colleague.
Read the information sheet and do the tasks below.
Incoterms® rules: information sheet
The Incoterms® rules are used by importers and exporters.
to define the costs and risks of international trade.
Transport costs
fan F term is used, the seller
is only responsible
for the
pre-carriage part of the goods’ journey to their destination.
In practice, this means that the seller
only loads the goods
on the first carrier's vehicle, eg. at the seller's premises,
or pays for transporting the goods to a convenient location
not too far away, e.g. a nearby port, airport or train station,
and loading the goods at that location, e.g. at the port
of shipment. The buyer
is then responsible for arranging
a contract
of carriage to transport the goods to their
destination and for unloading them when they arrive
Ifa C term is used, the seller pays
the costs of the main carriage to the destination but not of unloading
at the destination. Post-carriage is the buyer's responsibility.
In the case of a D term, the seller pays all transport costs until the goods have reached their destination.
Risks
With an F term, the seller bears the risk until the goods have been handed over to the first carrier, e.g
at the seller's premises, or in the case
of FOB until the goods are on board a ship at the port of shipment
With CPT and CIP, the risk to the seller is the same because it passes to the buyer when the goods have
been collected by the first carrier. In the case of CIP, the seller also insures the goods for the main carriage
but no longer bears any risk when they have been handed over
to the first carrier.
D terms cover all risks until the goods have reached their destination.
Import and export clearance
Export clearance (e.g. export licences, documentation) is arranged and paid for by the seller. Import
clearance (e.g. customs duty, import licences and documentation) is arranged and paid for by the buyer.
Erklären Sie mit Hilfe des Texts, ..
Rezer
stehen,
welche Transportkosten der Verkäufer bei einer F-Incoterms®-Klausel übernimmt.
Geben Sie zwei Beispiele an.
wer bei einer C-Incoterms®-Klausel die Kosten für den Haupttransport trägt.
wer bei einer C-Incoterms®-Klausel die Entladungskosten trägt.
welche Transportkosten der Käufer bei einer D-Incoterms®-Klausel trägt.
bis zu welchem Punkt der Verkäufer bei FOB das Risiko trägt.
bis zu welchem Punkt der Verkäufer bei CPT und CIP das Risiko trägt.
wer das Risiko bei einer D-Incoterms®-Klausel trägt.
wer für die Besorgung einer Einfuhrgenehmigung zuständig ist.
wer die Kosten einer Ausfuhrgenehmigung trägt.

--- Seite 71 ---
ocus on Business
You now have enough information to understand the definitions of the Incoterms® rules used in the
offers. Copy and complete the table below with data from the three definitions.
— FREE ON BOARD
(... named port of shipment)
The seller is not responsible for the main carriage of the goods. The seller delivers the goods at their
own expense and risk, in the customary packing, cleared for export, on board the vessel selected
by the buyer unless otherwise agreed, at the named port of shipment. Thereafter, the buyer bears
all the costs and risks of transporting
the goods to their destination.
FCA — FREE CARRIER (... named place of delivery) Multimodal transport
The seller is not responsible for the main carriage of the goods. The seller delivers the goods at their
own expense and risk, in the customary packing, cleared for export to the carrier nominated by
the buyer. The seller provides the commercial invoice and, if requested, a certificate of origin at
the buyer's expense. If the goods are collected at the seller's premises, the seller loads the goods
The seller bears the risks until the goods are in the custody of the first carrier. After that the
buyer bears all the costs and risks of transporting the goods to their destination.
CIP — CARRIAGE AND INSURANCE PAID TO (... named place of destination)
Multimodal transport The seller pays for the main carriage of the goods. The seller delivers the
goods in the customary packing, cleared for export to the carrier which they nominate. The seller
bears the risk until the goods have been delivered into the custody of the first carrier. The seller
pays the transport costs for the goods, including transport insurance, up to the named destination.
The buyer pays all import duties and taxes.

Commercial correspondence
You also find an explanation of terms of payment on your company's intranet
Terms
of payment
Before the buyer and seller sign a contract of sale they must first agree when and how payment will be made.
Ideally, the seller would like payment in advance before starting work on the order and the buyer would like
a long time to pay for the goods, so they can be sold before they are paid for. In practice, ifthe seller trusts the
customer, for example if the customer places regular orders, or if a new customer can show good references
from other sellers, the seller will give a credit period of perhaps 30, 60 or 90 days. Some trusted customers get
open account terms, which means that they pay for the goods at the end of the month or quarter. If the seller
doesn’t know or doesn't trust the customer, the terms of payment will be payment in advance, cash with
order (CWO) or payment by letter of credit (L/C), which means that the buyer’s bank guarantees payment.
The table shows some typical terms of payment and whether they are good or bad for the buyer and seller.

# Supply, deliver and ship
A company
that supplies goods makes them available
to other companies
or buyers. A supplier is
normally a manufacturer, wholesaler
or retailer.
A company that delivers goods collects them from the supplier and transports them to their destination
A company that offers this service is called a forwarder, freight forwarder or forwarding agent (all modes
of transport); a ha
is only involved in road transport.
A company
that ships goods sends
or transports them. Goods can be shipped by air, road, rail and sea

If an article is faulty, old, worn out, damaged,
broken or lost, a replacement is ordered
The replacement is identical to the old article.
If an article ordered is not available, for example
because it is out of stock
or no longer
manufactured, the supplier usually offers
a substitute. A substitute is similar

+ _ open account terms with monthly or quarterly settlement
10 days 2%, 30 days net

Yawith order, Ys on delivery, % within 30/60/90 days after delivery
ir German equivalents in box B.
In most cases,
a reminder is therefore sent to a regular and/or trusted customer. The first reminder is
a polite reference to the unpaid invoice and a request to pay soon. The second reminder is more forceful.
Itasks for an explanation and is an urgent request for payment. The third remainder, or final demand,
sets a deadline
and describes
the consequences of non-payment. tis normally addressed to

NON-VERBAL COMMUNICATION
Experts agree
that spoken language makes up only a small percentage
of how we communicate. The rest is the
non-verbal messages we give with our body: body language. Non-verbal messages are hard to hide because
they are shown automatically on our face (facial expressions) and by how we hold our body (posture).
online shopping
smart warehouse
riverless delivery van
delivery by drone
How often do you use e-commerce? Discuss this with a partner.
Facial expressions
The face shows a very wide range of reactions through the lips, mouth, eyebrows and eyes. The eyes are
known as the ‘windows to the soul’ and our pupils dilate (become bigger) to show positive emotion, such as
attraction, and contract (become smaller) to show negative emotion, such as anger. How rapidly
we blink
can show a number
of emotions, including stress. When our lips are pursed (pressed together tightly) they
show disapproval or frustration. When they are parted to show the teeth, they can express happiness
With your partner, make a list of the advantages and disadvantages of e-commerce. Which list is longer?
Many companies use a communication system called IVR.
(smile) or aggression (snarl). We bite our lips when we feel fear.
Posture
How we hold our body and what we do with our hands, arms and legs also say a lot about how we are feeling,
Open hands show that we are relaxed, whereas crossed arms and legs often mean that we are defensive
and unrelaxed. Standing with our feet apart means we are friendly and welcoming. The space
we leave
How can callers explain what they want?
Why do businesses use IVR?

DETROIT PEOPLE MOVER
The Detroit People Mover is an elevated railtrans-
portation service which provides an affordable
and entertaining ride through Downtown Detroit
for both tourists and commuters. Sections of the
circular rail line operate 45 feet above street level,
offering travelers panoramic views of the city. In
addition, each station is home
to beautiful public
artworks, so even waiting
for the train is a pleasure.
Convenient and good value, the service runs seven
days
a week.
WHERE CAN | FIND
A DPM STATION?
All thirteen People Mover stations are marked on
our map. Some stops are located within major
buildings in the Downtown area with public access.
The remaining stations are at street level and are
marked by brightly-colored cross beams. Each station
is announced on board the train prior to arrival
Everyone is welcome aboard the DPM, so every
station is accessible to disabled and elderly persons
via elevators and escalators as well as stairs.
Stations integrated into buildings:
Grand Circus Park (Woodward & Park)
Cadillac Center (Broadway & Gratiot)
Greektown (Attached to Jack Greektown Casino)
Millender Center
Renaissance Center
Financial District (Larned & Shelby)
Cobo Center
Street level stations:
Michigan Avenue
Times Square (Grand River & Park Ave.)
Broadway (Broadway & Leon R.St.)
Bricktown (Beaubien & Fort St.)
Joe Louis Arena
Fort-Cass

Für die Festivalbesucher soll als Unterkunftsmöglichkeit „Glamping“ angeboten werden.
Sie möchten wissen, was Glamping eigentlich ist, und finden im Internet einen informativen Artikel
Fassen Sie die wichtigsten Punkte des Artikels unter den angegebenen Überschriften stichwortartig
auf Deutsch zusammen.
Bedeutung des Wortes „Glamping“
verschiedene Zelttypen
"grundsätzliche Unterschiede zwischen
typische Ausstattung
Glamping und Camping
Stromversorgung und Beleuchtung
‘“GLAMPING
Glamourous camping for beginners
For many, camping
is associated with hard work, dirt and a terrible
night's sleep. ‘Glamping,’ a hybrid of the words ‘glamorous’ and
‘camping’ offers something much more comfortable. At our campsite,
you can enjoy
a relaxing experience while still appreciating
beautiful natural surroundings. Leave the heavy equipment at home
if you decide
to camp with us, you'll arrive to a pre-erected tent
your choice. Instead
of the commonplace
A-frame tent we have more
spacious options such as bell tents,
tipis and yurts. We've even
replaced sleeping bags by futons and silk sheets. For special occasions
like weddings
and in-company team-building weekends, we also offer
a range of stronger structures including shepherd's huts and gypsy
wagons for even more comfort. We choose the location for each of
our accommodation options very carefully, making sure that tents are
belltent |
pitched on level ground or on a platform to guarantee a peaceful
night's sleep. Each tent has access
to its own picnic area with cutlery
and tableware, as well as a fire pit with a private supply of firewood.
Showers
and toilets are available nearby, along with toiletries, hair
dryers and hot towels.
Though we provide these services, we still value the simplicity of the
camping experience. We believe that when the stress of a typical
camping
trip is removed, our customers have more time to fully enjoy
the nature around them. This is also the reason why our campsite is
‘off the grid,’ meaning
that there is no electricity available to charge
electronic devices. Not having
a mobile phone helps our campers
fully ‘switch off” and take a break from their busy everyday lives.
At night
the campsite has
a completely different feeling, lit only by
torches and firelight. We respect the simple pleasures in life and we
encourage our campers to do the same during their stay with us.
(315 words)

Event-Manager Ben Archer beruft eine Sitzung ein, um das Sicherheitskonzept des Festivals zu
besprechen, und bittet um Beiträge. Sie finden einen Artikel über Sicherheit bei Massenveranstaltungen
in deutscher Sprache im Internet.
Fassen Sie unter den angegebenen Überschriften die wichtigsten Punkte des Artikels in englischer
Sprache zusammen.
Safer spaces for particular
groups
+ Women's campsites
Rapid-response security teams
Wie schafft man mehr Sicherheit,
und wer schreitet schon vorbildlich voran?
1. Safe(r) Spaces
Safe(r) Spaces sind abgetrennte Bereiche, zu denen nur Menschen Zugang haben, die sich diskriminiert
fühlen oder Diskriminierung befürchten. Viele Festivalveranstalter öffnen diese Bereiche fiir Queers,
Transgender, Frauen, non-binäre und Menschen mit Behinderung. Diese sollen die Veranstaltung hier in
Ruhe und sicher genießen können - ganz und gar sorglos. Das Glastonbury Festival in Großbritannien,
hat 2016 erstmals den sogenannten „Sisterhood“-Bereich geöffnet - ein Safe Space auf dem Festival-
gelände. Die Teilnehmerinnen waren begeistert und sprachen von einmaligen Emotionen und Erfahrun-
gen in dem abgetrennten Bereich.
2. Frauen-Camping
Das Nova Rock Festival in Österreich bietet dieses Jahr (2019) erstmalig einen abgetrennten Campingplatz
nur für Frauen an. Dafür meldet Frau sich ganz einfach über die Webseite an. Die Idee ist, dass Frauen
sich im Camp nachts wie tagsüber sorglos aufhalten und frei entfalten können, denn immer mehr
Frauen melden,
dass sie das auf dem gemischten Campingplatz nicht tun.
3. Awareness-Teams
Immer mehr Festivals setzen auch auf Awareness-Teams. Das sind Sicherheits-Teams, die exklusiv dafür
da sind, einzuspringen und beizustehen, sobald sie etwas sehen, auf etwas hingewiesen werden oder
direkt um Hilfe gebeten werden. Um es potentiellen Opfern leichter zu machen, selbst um Hilfe zu bitten
und auf sich aufmerksam zu machen, gibt es ein Codewort. Auf dem Hurricane Festival fragt man zum
Beispiel ‚Wo geht's denn nach Panama?". Die Sicherheitsleute wissen dann sofort Bescheid und bringen
die betroffene Person ohne weitere Nachfragen direkt an einen sicheren Ort - zum Beispiel zu einem
Safe Space.
(250 words)
Source: wwweventbrite de/blog/sicherheit-auf-deinem-festival/
Sie sind im irischen Cork mit den Vorbereitungen fiir das Kelly Farm Music Festival beschaftigt.

Hilfe bei der Beschaffung. Sie notieren seine Wünsche auf Deutsch, recherchieren im Internet, rufen bei
einem geeigneten Lieferanten an und geben für Kelly eine Bestellung auf.

5 FURTHER FOCUS
Preventing digital overload must become part
of employee well-being programmes
Digital technology, in particular
the smartphone,
has transformed the way
we do business
and conduct
our social lives. This has opened up the opportunity for flexible working, but with it a culture has
developed where employees increasingly feel the need to be available around the clock
Twenty-four hours a day we are bombarded with endless interruptions through emails, texts, alerts and
instant messaging. For many, it is far too easy to be reactive, wasting
time on relatively useless tasks
and interactions, remaining busy but not productive. Research released this year found that millions of
people are now seeking a break from their technology. The majority of us admit to being “hooked” on
our smartphones, with one-third saying they have difficulty disconnecting at all
There is even an official term for this behaviour. The Collins Dictionary defines "nomophobia” as “a state
of stress caused by having no access or being unable to use one’s mobile phone’.
So how can companies provide support and guidarice in how to better manage digital technology usage
in order to Safeguard the well-being and work-life balance of their staff so they can perform to their best
and build resilience?
One route would be to follow France, where the government has introduced a new “right to disconnect
to ban workers from sending or replying to emails outside of working hours.
Starting to use technology in a more mindful way is the first step. The following are a few tips to give
employees about how to achieve this:
1 Leave your phone at the bedroom door
Leaving your phone off while you get up, dressed and eat breakfast makes for a better start to the day.
2 Turn off notifications and use “flight mode”
Turn the default notifications off. Make use of “flight mode” and stop texts and calls coming through.
3 Use good old-fashioned pen and paper
Carry a small notepad and pen with you and every time you want
to look something up online, resist the
temptation to do it there and then. Use your list to go online only a few times a day.
4 Be mindful and reclaim the pause in your day
Resist the temptation to automatically reach for your phone every time you have a free moment.
Read a book, look out of the window, or just close your eyes and breathe.
(400 words)
Source: This article by Anna Kotwinski of Shine Online was originally published in Occupational Health &
Wellbeing magazine, 01 February, 2017. Occupational Health & Wellbeing is published by DVV Media.

Here are 10 tips for victims of cyberbullying.
Don't reply: Replying can make the problem worse.
Collect evidence: Save screenshots and emails.
Block the cyberbully: Change your contact details only share them with friends.
Report the cyberbully to the provider: Some websites can block the cyberbully and delete posts.
Tell other people: Don't suffer alone. Get support from people you trust.
Get expert help: Family members often overreact, but a counsellor can help you get your
confidence back
7 Any contact with the cyberbully should
be via a mediator, not your parents: A well-informed
outsider can mediate better than overemotional parents.
8 Tell your school/college:
Talk to teachers about what to do.
9. Tell the police in extreme cases: Spreading lies about people, and insulting and humiliating
them online is illegal. Consider legal action.
10 Don't just stop using your phone and/or the internet: Others will still see the posts even if you
don't, and it won't help to cut yourself off from friends and family.

ocus on Business
You are getting work experience at a large furniture retailing chain called DIY Homemaker Ltd with its
headquarters in Dublin, Ireland. You attend an in-service training workshop about how to deal with
everyday problems
with colleagues.
The workshop leader gives you a handout with a diagram,
Nobody wants conflict at work but it's part of life and can be dealt with if you follow some simple
guidelines. Above all, conflicts must be acknowledged. If they are ignored, they will grow and break out
sooner or later, perhaps when its too late. Show respect to your colleagues by speaking less and listening
more. Don't tell people what to do. Instead, ask them what they want to do. Give praise whenever possible.
Apologize if you have done something wrong, Follow the six steps below in a conflict situation.
Follow these six steps to solving conflicts in the workplace:
‘sk the other person
Focus on facts, noton people.
to suggest a good time and
—> + Say There isa problem because...”
place to talk.
+ Don't say You always...”
Identify the problem.
+ Find out where you agree
and disagree.
Listen to the other person.
<— + Letthem talk.
+ Don't interrupt them.
Discuss
the future.
‘Agree on a solution.
Ls + Don'tconcentrate on problems © >
+ Ortrytofind a date to meet
in the past.
again.
Step 1: If you give the other person the freedom to choose when and where to meet to discuss the
problem, you show your goodwill because they will see that you are willing to change your plans to
find a solution. You will produce
a bad feeling in the other person if you are only willing
to meet when
and where you choose.
Step 2: You’ statements, such as“You never listen’ or ‘You don't help, are very dangerous because they
stress that the other person is the problem. To find a solution, focus on facts not personalities. Say ‘The
goods went to the wrong address’ and not ‘You sent the goods to the wrong address’
Step 3: Listening is a skill. You may think you already know everything, but perhaps the other person
knows something you don't. Listen carefully, give the other person time and don't interrupt. Ask
questions at the end to make sure you have understood and then summarize what the other person
has said.
Step 4: First summarize the points where you agree and check with the other person. Now summarize
the points where you disagree and modify your summary until you both agree on the areas of conflict.
Dealing with conflicts at work
Step 5: Try not to focus on the past. Look forward and develop a plan of action for each area of conflict.
Step 6: Agree a date to meet again and review the progress of the solution(s) you both suggested. At
the next meeting, congratulate each other when you see that progress has been made, no matter how
small. If necessary, continue or modify your plan(s) of action and meet again.
(425 words)

Protection against Discrimination in Germany
A Guide for Refugees and New Immigrants (English)
What is discrimination?
Discrimination means that one person is treated worse than another person, for example because
ofa disability
or their origins. Discrimination is prohibited in Germany.
In which areas of life does this protection against discrimination apply?
The General Equal Treatment
Act protects people from discrimination in two areas: working
life and
in specific
cases of day-to-day life. Working life means that no one may be discriminated against:
when applying for a job
with respect to working conditions
with respect
to pay
with respect
to promotion or terminations
For example, this means that people working in an enterprise may not be paid less for their work,
simply because they come from another country.
On the job and in your profession
In Germany, every person is protected from discrimination with respect to access to work, working con
ditions
and terminations. This protection also applies to professional training, for example internships...
Applying for a job and taking up employment
Finding work is very important, particularly for persons
who are new in Germany. Unfortunately, itis
precisely in this context that discrimination occurs frequently. In some cases, persons with a foreign:
sounding name are less likely
to be invited to a job interview.
This
You can do something
about this type of discrimination. No person may be discriminated against,
when applying
for a job, on the grounds of ethnic origin, gender, religion or belief, disability, age or
sexual identity
discrimination!
‘Muslim women wearing headscarves
‘Muslim women wearing headscarves also experience discrimination when job hunting. Very often,
they are rejected with the justification that customers or other employees in the firm have a problem
with the headscarf
This is not allowed! No person seeking employment may be rejected because of their religion! Excep
tions are made only for employers
who are funded by a religious community. Women who are affect-
ed by this sort of discrimination should therefore seek counselling
at all costs.
(339 words)
Source: Antidiskriminierungsstelle des Bundes (www.antidiskriminierungsstelle.de/SharedDocs/Downloads/
DE/publikationen/Refugees/Fluechtlingsbroschuere_englisch.pdf)

PARTNER FILES
Group A
Read the text and complete the following tasks.
Asa group, identify 4-5 questions that you can ask your classmates in order to compare Generation Z
in Germany with young American consumers.
Each member of your group should take a question and survey the rest of your class.
Come back together as a group to prepare and present your results as a presentation or gallery walk.
Where do they shop?
People think that Generation Z do all their shopping online nowadays, but in fact 60% of American Gen
Zers still ike to go to traditional bricks-and-mortar stores. How they differ from older shoppers is that
they combine online research with a visit to a store. As a result, they do not hang around shopping
malls all day, but go in knowing what they want, buy it and leave. Clever retailers have discovered this,
and the really innovative ones have blended the online and the offline world by putting more interactive
touchscreens in the stores and harnessing technology such as virtual and augmented reality to make
the real-world shopping experience more attractive for shoppers. Generation Z consumers do not like
to wait. They prefer fast and efficient assistance in-store, rather than friendly service, and most like
self-service checkouts with electronic
payment systems — cutting
out the human element altogether.
A majority prefer the option of shopping online and picking up their goods in a store while two-thirds
say they would pay alittle bit more for delivery within one hour.
Partner B
Analyse the company below and share your information with your partners.
Silverlining Cloud Services
Silverlining are an IT firm founded ten years ago. They design apps for a variety of computer operating
systems according to the requirements of their clients: businesses and educational organizations.
They were bought by a global business software company and now also offer cloud data hosting and
analysis
to their corporate clients.

them, so this generation responds well to advertising campaigns they find funny. They are three times
more likely to buy a product due to clever campaigns than older generations. They are not as easily
cows
persuaded by glamourous celebrities in advertisements. Three-quarters
trust the opinions of family and
friends more than the endorsements by Hollywood actors or pop stars. They are willing
to share their

How important is the product?
Product quality is important to Generation Z-two-thirds say that quality is a priority when deciding
what to buy. And they do not just take manufacturers’ promises as guarantees of quality. Three-quarters
Partner B
say they read product reviews, watch unboxing videos online and consider friends’ opinions when
judging quality. 60% say they buy brands that reflect their personality and 40% say they are willing
pay more for a brand they believe in. But that loyalty isn’t a guarantee that Gen Zers will stick with a
brand. Today's young consumers are not as loyal
to brands as their older counterparts. Only 16% shop
ata single store for their clothing and fashion needs. Sustainability is also
a priority for this market.
Three-quarters of them consider
the environmental impact of product manufacture and such things
as packaging. They are also willing to pay more for products and services which are eco-friendly —
packaging-free goods and organic food, for example. Access
to products and services is more important
to the American Gen Z than ownership of the actual products. Accessing products and services instead
of buying them also means less worry about repairing broken belongings, replacing stolen items or
disposing of e-waste.

How price conscious are they?
Older people think that the young do not appreciate the value of money, but Generation Z are quite
price conscious and are willing
to shop around for the best deals. Gen Zers are experts at finding special
offers online and taking advantage of mobile apps that offer money-off vouchers. While 30% say they
use money-off coupons and vouchers, 73% say they join loyalty schemes if they receive discounted prices.
They are also open to innovative pricing models. Only 38% of them still listen to music on CDs with the
rest streaming
their music either through free ad-based apps or subscription-based premium services.
This subscription model has spread to movie and TV streaming, gaming, computer software, e-books,
fashion and even household goods and food. 73% of Gen Z consumers say they are open to ‘renting’
clothes rather than buying,
and a slightly lower number (71%) are willing
to sign up to replenishment
programmes — receiving a new supply of batteries every two months, for example.
Partner C
Analyse the company below and share your information with your partners.
Sensitiva
Sensitiva manufacture a wide range of sensors and cameras for industry. These range from infrared sensors
for military aircraft to optical cameras for quality testing in the pharmaceutical industry. Five years ago,
they bought a software company specializing in artificial intelligence and can now provide ‘smart’ sensors
such as facial and handwriting recognition which are linked to Sensitiva’s Analysor supercomputer.

GLOSSARY OF BUSINESS TERMS
In the EU, there are two basic types of company,
the private limited company (GB: Ltd; German: GmbH)
and the public limited company (GB: plc; German: AG). In the USA and Canada there are three types
‘of company, as follows:
Incorporated company (Inc.) There is no exact equivalent of an incorporated company in the EU
‘incorporated’ simply means ‘registered as a company. It does not say anything about ownership or
liability, or capitalization.
Close corporation (Corp.) This is the North American equivalent
of the British Ltd and German GmbH.
Close corporations have a small number of shareholders (here: Gesellschafter/in) and do not offer
their shares on the stock market (Börse),
+ Open corporation (Corp) The North American equivalent
of the British PLC and German AG. Open
corporations usually have numerous shareholders (here: Aktionär/in), often other corporations,
and sell their shares on the stock market.
In South Africa, Australia and New Zealand the equivalents of the British Ltd and plc are proprietary
limited company (Pty Ltd) and proprietary company (Pty).
Asole trader (USA: sole proprietor) is the single owner of a company and takes all the decisions.
He/She gets all the profit from the company, but also bears all the risks.
‘As trade becomes more and more global, goods travel further and further, crossing geographical, cultural
and language barriers on their way. For this reason it is essential that importers and exporters agree to use
the same terms of reference.
In 1936 the International Chamber
of Commerce in Paris invented a set of International Commercial Terms
(Incoterms® rules) to define importers’ and exporters’ rights and obligations, such as transport costs, risk,
insurance, customs duty, documentation, loading and unloading. Since then the Incoterms® rules have
been revised eight times to keep up with developments in the field of international trade and translated
into many different languages. The last revision was in 2020. There are now eleven Incoterms® rules, seven
of which can be used for any mode or combined modes of transport, e.g. truck, train, ship or rail. The other
four are used for ship or inland waterway transport only.
Rules for any mode or modes of transport
EXW (EX WORKS)
Ab Werk
The seller makes the goods available at his premises. The buyer bears all
the costs and risks of transporting the goods to their destination
FCA (FREE CARRIER)
Frei Frachtführer
The seller loads the goods on board the first! carrier's vehicle. The buyer
bears all the costs and risks of transporting the goods to their destination.
